\section{Implementation-Ready Form of the Corrected Toy Family Operator}

\section{1. Fixed data of the toy problem}

We keep the fixed three-defect background
\begin{equation}
P_0(x)=\sum_{A=1}^3 p_A(x)\, z_A z_A^\dagger,
\qquad
p_A(x)=\frac{w_A(x)}{W(x)},
\qquad
w_A(x)=\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-X_A)^2}{2R^2}\right],
\qquad
W(x)=\sum_{B=1}^3 w_B(x),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
X_1=-1.5,\qquad X_2=0,\qquad X_3=1.8.
\end{equation}

Let the Gaussian basis be
\begin{equation}
b_\mu(x)=\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-Y_\mu)^2}{2\sigma_b^2}\right],
\qquad \mu=1,\dots,N_b.
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu\nu}:=\frac{Y_\mu+Y_\nu}{2},
\qquad
D_{\mu\nu}:=Y_\mu-Y_\nu.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
b_\mu(x)b_\nu(x)
=
\exp\!\left[-\frac{D_{\mu\nu}^2}{4\sigma_b^2}\right]
\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2}{\sigma_b^2}\right].
\end{equation}

We also fix a traceless diagonal sector spurion
\begin{equation}
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(t_1,t_2,t_3),
\qquad
t_1+t_2+t_3=0,
\end{equation}
and define
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d(x):=\mathrm{Tr}(T_dP_0(x))=\sum_{A=1}^3 t_A p_A(x).
\end{equation}

The Hermitian corrected toy operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\,\Pi_d(x)
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact implementation formula for \(\Pi_d'(x)\)}

Since
\begin{equation}
p_A'(x)=\frac{1}{R^2}p_A(x)\bigl(X_A-\bar X(x)\bigr),
\qquad
\bar X(x):=\sum_{B=1}^3 p_B(x)X_B,
\end{equation}
we have
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)=\sum_A t_A p_A'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}\sum_A t_A p_A(x)\bigl(X_A-\bar X(x)\bigr).
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,p_A(x)p_B(x).
}
\end{equation}

This second form is numerically and conceptually superior because it makes the link structure explicit.

\section{3. Overlap and local Hessian basis}

The overlap matrix is
\begin{equation}
S_{\mu\nu}=\int dx\, b_\mu(x)b_\nu(x)
=
\sqrt{\pi}\sigma_b
\exp\!\left[-\frac{D_{\mu\nu}^2}{4\sigma_b^2}\right].
\end{equation}

The local toy Hessian basis is obtained from the generalized eigenvalue problem
\begin{equation}
Lc_A=\varepsilon_A S c_A,
\end{equation}
where \(L_{\mu\nu}=\int dx\, b_\mu \mathcal L_{\rm loc} b_\nu\).
Let
\begin{equation}
C=(c_1,c_2,c_3)
\end{equation}
be the three selected family columns, normalized such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^\dagger S C=I_3.
}
\end{equation}

Then the family Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger Y^{(d)} C,
}
\end{equation}
where \(Y^{(d)}\) is the matrix of \(\delta H_d^{\rm herm}\) in the Gaussian basis.

\section{4. Exact Gaussian-basis matrix elements}

\subsection{4.1. Potential contribution}

The potential part is
\begin{equation}
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\int dx\, b_\mu(x)\Pi_d(x)b_\nu(x).
\end{equation}
Using the Gaussian product identity,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\,
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int dx\,
e^{-(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2/\sigma_b^2}\Pi_d(x).
}
\end{equation}

Introduce the dimensionless quadrature variable
\begin{equation}
x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u,
\qquad
dx=\sigma_b\,du.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\,\sigma_b\,
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} du\, e^{-u^2}\,
\Pi_d(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
}
\end{equation}

This is the preferred numerical form.

\subsection{4.2. Derivative contribution}

Define
\begin{equation}
K:=\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\}.
\end{equation}
Then the exact Hermitian matrix element is
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
-\frac{i\kappa_d}{2}
\int dx\, \Pi_d'(x)\bigl(b_\mu b_\nu'-b_\mu' b_\nu\bigr).
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
b_\mu'(x)= -\frac{x-Y_\mu}{\sigma_b^2}b_\mu(x),
\end{equation}
one finds
\begin{equation}
b_\mu b_\nu'-b_\mu' b_\nu
=
\frac{Y_\nu-Y_\mu}{\sigma_b^2}b_\mu b_\nu.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_b^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int dx\,
e^{-(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2/\sigma_b^2}\Pi_d'(x).
}
\end{equation}
After the same rescaling \(x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_b}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} du\, e^{-u^2}\,
\Pi_d'(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\mu}=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Fully expanded link form of \(K_{\mu\nu}\)}

Substituting the exact link decomposition of \(\Pi_d'(x)\),
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)=\frac{1}{R^2}\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)p_A(x)p_B(x),
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,
J_{\mu\nu}^{AB},
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\mu\nu}^{AB}
:=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}du\, e^{-u^2}\,
p_A(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)\,
p_B(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
}
\end{equation}

Thus the corrected Gaussian-basis matrix element is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Y_{\mu\nu}^{(d)}
=
g_d\,\sigma_b\,
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int du\, e^{-u^2}\Pi_d(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)
+
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)J_{\mu\nu}^{AB}.
}
\end{equation}

This is the final implementation-ready formula.

\section{6. Stable evaluation of the profiles}

For numerical stability, one should evaluate \(p_A(x)\) via shifted exponentials. Let
\begin{equation}
m(x):=\max_A\left[-\frac{(x-X_A)^2}{2R^2}\right].
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\tilde w_A(x):=
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{(x-X_A)^2}{2R^2}-m(x)
\right],
\qquad
p_A(x)=\frac{\tilde w_A(x)}{\sum_B \tilde w_B(x)}.
\end{equation}
This avoids underflow in the tails.

After this, \(\Pi_d(x)\) and \(\Pi_d'(x)\) are evaluated from
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d(x)=\sum_A t_A p_A(x),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)=\frac{1}{R^2}\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)p_A(x)p_B(x).
\end{equation}

\section{7. Family projection in component form}

Let
\begin{equation}
C_{\mu A}=(c_A)_\mu,
\qquad
A=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(H_d^{\rm fam})_{AB}
=
\sum_{\mu,\nu}
C_{\mu A}^*\,Y_{\mu\nu}^{(d)}\,C_{\nu B}.
}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
d_A=(H_d^{\rm fam})_{AA},
\qquad
h_{AB}=(H_d^{\rm fam})_{AB}\quad (A\neq B).
\end{equation}

This is the exact quantity to be used for the CKM extraction formulas.

\section{8. Why the corrected operator suppresses \(h_{13}\)}

The derivative part is controlled by
\begin{equation}
J_{\mu\nu}^{AB}
=
\int du\, e^{-u^2} p_A(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)p_B(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
\end{equation}
But \(p_Ap_B\) is localized near the midpoint
\begin{equation}
m_{AB}:=\frac{X_A+X_B}{2},
\end{equation}
with intrinsic penalty
\begin{equation}
\sim e^{-D_{AB}^2/(4R^2)},
\qquad
D_{AB}:=|X_A-X_B|.
\end{equation}
At the same time the Gaussian basis product contributes
\begin{equation}
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}.
\end{equation}

Hence the transport between family modes centered near \(A\) and \(B\) receives the double suppression
\begin{equation}
|h_{AB}^{(K)}|
\sim
e^{-D_{AB}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
e^{-D_{AB}^2/(4R^2)}
\times
\text{(order-one link coefficient)}.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\frac{|h_{13}|}{|h_{12}|}
\lesssim
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{D_{13}^2-D_{12}^2}{4\sigma_b^2}
\right]
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{D_{13}^2-D_{12}^2}{4R^2}
\right],
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\frac{|h_{13}|}{|h_{23}|}
\lesssim
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{D_{13}^2-D_{23}^2}{4\sigma_b^2}
\right]
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{D_{13}^2-D_{23}^2}{4R^2}
\right].
\end{equation}

For the present centers,
\begin{equation}
D_{12}=1.5,\qquad D_{23}=1.8,\qquad D_{13}=3.3,
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
D_{13}^2-D_{12}^2=8.64,\qquad D_{13}^2-D_{23}^2=7.65.
\end{equation}
Thus the direct \(1\text{--}3\) channel is strongly penalized unless both \(R\) and \(\sigma_b\) are unnaturally large.

\section{9. Precise computational pipeline}

The corrected toy CKM pipeline is now:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Fix \(R,\sigma_b,g_d,\kappa_d\) and the Gaussian centers \(Y_\mu\).
\item Build \(S_{\mu\nu}\) and \(L_{\mu\nu}\), solve
\[
Lc_A=\varepsilon_A S c_A,
\qquad
C^\dagger S C=I_3.
\]
\item For each pair \((\mu,\nu)\), compute \(M_{\mu\nu}\), \(D_{\mu\nu}\).
\item Evaluate \(p_A(x)\), \(\Pi_d(x)\), \(\Pi_d'(x)\) on the quadrature points
\[
x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u.
\]
\item Assemble \(V_{\mu\nu}\) and \(K_{\mu\nu}\), hence
\[
Y^{(d)}=V+K.
\]
\item Project to the family space:
\[
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger Y^{(d)} C.
\]
\item Read off
\[
d_1,d_2,d_3,\qquad h_{12},h_{23},h_{13}.
\]
\item Only after this, apply the CKM extraction formulas.
\end{enumerate}

\section{10. What is now closed and what is still open}

What is closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the corrected toy operator has a unique Hermitian definition and a unique implementation formula.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the Gaussian-basis matrix elements reduce to explicit one-dimensional weighted quadratures.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the derivative part is exactly a sum over pairwise defect links and structurally suppresses }1\text{--}3.
}
\end{equation}

What is still open:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual CKM numbers depend on the chosen sector spurion, the local Hessian basis, and the parameter point.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a robust nonzero physical CKM phase is not yet guaranteed at this one-spurion toy level.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The corrected toy down-sector operator is now fully closed in a Hermitian implementation-ready form:
\begin{equation}
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\,\Pi_d(x)
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\},
\qquad
\Pi_d(x)=\sum_A t_A p_A(x),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
p_A(x)=\frac{e^{-(x-X_A)^2/(2R^2)}}{\sum_B e^{-(x-X_B)^2/(2R^2)}}.
\end{equation}

Its derivative profile admits the exact link decomposition
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,p_A(x)p_B(x),
\end{equation}
which shows that the corrected transport term is an exact sum of pairwise link-localized contributions.

In the Gaussian basis \(b_\mu(x)=e^{-(x-Y_\mu)^2/(2\sigma_b^2)}\), the projected matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\,\sigma_b\,e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\int du\,e^{-u^2}\Pi_d(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u),
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)
\int du\,e^{-u^2}p_A(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)p_B(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
Y^{(d)}=V+K,
\qquad
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger Y^{(d)} C,
\qquad
C^\dagger S C=I_3.
\end{equation}

The corrected operator therefore reduces the toy CKM problem to explicit one-dimensional quadratures. Its structural consequence is that off-diagonal transport is controlled by link-localized pair factors \(p_Ap_B\), and the direct \(1\text{--}3\) channel is doubly suppressed by both basis overlap and background link overlap:
\begin{equation}
|h_{13}|
\ll
|h_{12}|,\ |h_{23}|
\end{equation}
in the localized-family regime.

Thus the operator-level ambiguity is removed. The remaining open problem is no longer how to define the toy operator, but which parameter point and sector spurion produce the observed CKM magnitudes and a nontrivial physical phase.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Viable Spurion and the Natural Hierarchy Window}

\section{1. Generic diagonal spurion and exact link coefficients}

Let the down-sector spurion be a generic traceless diagonal matrix
\begin{equation}
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(t_1,t_2,t_3),
\qquad
t_1+t_2+t_3=0.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d(x)=\mathrm{Tr}(T_dP_0(x))=\sum_{A=1}^3 t_A p_A(x),
\end{equation}
and the exact derivative profile is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,p_A(x)p_B(x).
\end{equation}

Hence the three direct link coefficients are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{12}=\frac{1}{R^2}(t_1-t_2)(X_1-X_2),
\qquad
\Lambda_{23}=\frac{1}{R^2}(t_2-t_3)(X_2-X_3),
\qquad
\Lambda_{13}=\frac{1}{R^2}(t_1-t_3)(X_1-X_3).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
t_A=t_B
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{the direct derivative link }A\text{--}B\text{ vanishes identically.}
}
\end{equation}

This is an exact statement, not an approximation.

\section{2. Why the previously convenient spurion is not viable as the first CKM toy spurion}

Consider
\begin{equation}
T_d^{\rm deg}\propto \mathrm{diag}(2,-1,-1).
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
t_2=t_3,
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{23}=0.
\end{equation}
Thus the corrected derivative operator contains no direct \(2\text{--}3\) transport term:
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
(t_1-t_2)(X_1-X_2)p_1p_2
+
(t_1-t_3)(X_1-X_3)p_1p_3
\Big].
\end{equation}

Hence any resulting \(h_{23}\) must arise only indirectly through basis mixing and/or the potential piece. This does not make the spurion mathematically inconsistent, but it makes it a poor first candidate for a clean CKM hierarchy study, because one of the nearest-neighbor transport channels is removed at the operator level.

\section{3. Minimal viable nondegenerate spurion}

The simplest traceless diagonal spurion with all pair differences nonzero is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_d^{\rm min}=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
t_1-t_2=1,
\qquad
t_2-t_3=1,
\qquad
t_1-t_3=2.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d(x)=p_1(x)-p_3(x),
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
(X_1-X_2)p_1p_2
+
(X_2-X_3)p_2p_3
+
2(X_1-X_3)p_1p_3
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

For the fixed defect centers
\begin{equation}
X_1=-1.5,\qquad X_2=0,\qquad X_3=1.8,
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
-\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1p_2
+
1.8\,p_2p_3
+
6.6\,p_1p_3
\Big].
\end{equation}

The direct \(1\text{--}3\) coefficient is indeed larger at the bare coefficient level. However, its associated pair profile \(p_1p_3\) is much more strongly suppressed by the larger separation \(D_{13}=3.3\). Thus the correct comparison is not coefficient-only, but coefficient times link overlap.

\section{4. Localized-family estimate for the derivative matrix elements}

The exact Gaussian-basis derivative matrix element is
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)
e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,
J_{\mu\nu}^{AB},
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
J_{\mu\nu}^{AB}
=
\int du\, e^{-u^2}p_A(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)p_B(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
\end{equation}

In the localized-family regime, after projection to the family basis, the leading direct \(A\text{--}B\) derivative mixing takes the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|h_{AB}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N\,
|\kappa_d|\,
|t_A-t_B|\,
D_{AB}^2\,
e^{-\alpha D_{AB}^2},
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D_{AB}=|X_A-X_B|,
\qquad
\alpha:=\frac{1}{4\sigma_*^2}+\frac{1}{4R^2},
\end{equation}
and \(\sigma_*\) is the effective family-mode width after projection.

This is not the exact matrix element, but it is the correct asymptotic scaling law in the localized regime. The factor \(D_{AB}^2\) comes from one factor of \(X_A-X_B\) in the derivative spurion and one factor of \(Y_\mu-Y_\nu\sim X_A-X_B\) in the transport matrix element.

\section{5. Natural hierarchy conditions for the minimal spurion}

For
\begin{equation}
T_d^{\rm min}=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1),
\end{equation}
the asymptotic direct-link amplitudes scale as
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 1\cdot D_{12}^2 e^{-\alpha D_{12}^2},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|h_{23}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 1\cdot D_{23}^2 e^{-\alpha D_{23}^2},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|h_{13}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 2\cdot D_{13}^2 e^{-\alpha D_{13}^2}.
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
D_{12}=1.5,\qquad D_{23}=1.8,\qquad D_{13}=3.3,
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 2.25\, e^{-2.25\alpha},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|h_{23}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 3.24\, e^{-3.24\alpha},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|h_{13}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d| \cdot 21.78\, e^{-10.89\alpha}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.1. Condition for \( |h_{12}|>|h_{23}| \)}

We require
\begin{equation}
2.25\, e^{-2.25\alpha}
>
3.24\, e^{-3.24\alpha}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
e^{0.99\alpha}>\frac{3.24}{2.25}=1.44.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>\alpha_{12>23}:=\frac{\ln(1.44)}{0.99}\approx 0.368.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.2. Condition for \( |h_{23}|>|h_{13}| \)}

We require
\begin{equation}
3.24\, e^{-3.24\alpha}
>
21.78\, e^{-10.89\alpha}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
e^{7.65\alpha}>\frac{21.78}{3.24}=6.72.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>\alpha_{23>13}:=\frac{\ln(6.72)}{7.65}\approx 0.249.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.3. Condition for \( |h_{12}|>|h_{13}| \)}

We require
\begin{equation}
2.25\, e^{-2.25\alpha}
>
21.78\, e^{-10.89\alpha}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
e^{8.64\alpha}>\frac{21.78}{2.25}=9.68.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>\alpha_{12>13}:=\frac{\ln(9.68)}{8.64}\approx 0.263.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Natural hierarchy window}

Combining the three inequalities, a sufficient condition for
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}^{(K)}|>|h_{23}^{(K)}|>|h_{13}^{(K)}|
\end{equation}
is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>\alpha_*:=0.368.
}
\end{equation}

Since
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\frac{1}{4\sigma_*^2}+\frac{1}{4R^2},
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{1}{4\sigma_*^2}+\frac{1}{4R^2}>0.368.
}
\end{equation}

For example, if
\begin{equation}
R=\sigma_*=1,
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\frac14+\frac14=0.5,
\end{equation}
which lies safely inside the hierarchy window.

Thus, for the minimal spurion \(T_d^{\rm min}=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1)\), the desired ordering
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|
}
\end{equation}
is not a fine-tuned accident. It appears naturally once the family modes and the defect links are sufficiently localized.

\section{7. Consequence for the corrected toy program}

The corrected toy program should therefore not start from the degenerate spurion
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{diag}(2,-1,-1),
\end{equation}
because that choice eliminates the direct \(2\text{--}3\) derivative link at the operator level.

The correct first nondegenerate run is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
}
\end{equation}
With this choice,
\begin{enumerate}
\item all three direct derivative links are present,
\item the two nearest-neighbor links have equal spurion strength,
\item the long link \(1\text{--}3\) is still strongly suppressed by geometry,
\item and there is a natural localization window in which
\[
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{8. Honest status of the CP phase at this stage}

At this stage, the corrected toy Hamiltonian takes the form
\begin{equation}
H_d^{\rm fam}=D+R+iA,
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D=\text{real diagonal},\qquad
R=\text{real symmetric off-diagonal part from }V,\qquad
A=\text{real antisymmetric part from }K.
\end{equation}
Hence \(H_d^{\rm fam}\) is a generic complex Hermitian matrix.

Therefore no symmetry forces all off-diagonal entries to be simultaneously real. However, it is still not yet proven here that
\begin{equation}
\Im(h_{12}h_{23}h_{31})\neq 0
\end{equation}
for the fixed toy background and chosen parameters. That must be checked explicitly after the full family projection. So the correct statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a physical CKM phase is now allowed generically, but not yet rigorously guaranteed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

For the Hermitian corrected toy operator
\begin{equation}
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\,\Pi_d(x)
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\},
\qquad
\Pi_d(x)=\sum_A t_A p_A(x),
\end{equation}
the exact derivative link coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{AB}=\frac{1}{R^2}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B).
\end{equation}
Therefore any diagonal spurion with \(t_A=t_B\) removes the direct derivative link \(A\text{--}B\) identically.

In particular, the previously convenient degenerate spurion
\begin{equation}
T_d\propto \mathrm{diag}(2,-1,-1)
\end{equation}
satisfies \(t_2=t_3\), so the direct \(2\text{--}3\) derivative link vanishes exactly. This makes it a poor first candidate for a clean CKM toy computation.

The simplest nondegenerate viable choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
}
\end{equation}
For this spurion, all three direct derivative links are present:
\begin{equation}
t_1-t_2=1,\qquad t_2-t_3=1,\qquad t_1-t_3=2.
\end{equation}
Thus the two nearest-neighbor links have equal spurion strength, while the long \(1\text{--}3\) link remains geometrically suppressed.

In the localized-family regime, the direct derivative matrix elements scale as
\begin{equation}
|h_{AB}^{(K)}|
\asymp
\mathcal N |\kappa_d|\, |t_A-t_B|\, D_{AB}^2 e^{-\alpha D_{AB}^2},
\qquad
\alpha=\frac{1}{4\sigma_*^2}+\frac{1}{4R^2}.
\end{equation}
Using the fixed toy separations
\begin{equation}
D_{12}=1.5,\qquad D_{23}=1.8,\qquad D_{13}=3.3,
\end{equation}
one finds that a sufficient condition for the natural hierarchy
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|
\end{equation}
is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha>0.368.
}
\end{equation}

Hence, with the minimal viable spurion \(T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1)\), the desired CKM-like ordering is not a fine-tuned accident but a natural consequence of sufficiently localized family modes and defect links.

What is now closed is the operator-level choice of the first correct nondegenerate spurion and the natural hierarchy window. What remains open is the explicit numerical evaluation of the full projected family Hamiltonian \(H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger Y^{(d)}C\) and the verification of a nonzero rephasing-invariant phase \(\Im(h_{12}h_{23}h_{31})\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal-Spurion Specialization and Execution-Ready Family Hamiltonian}

\section{1. Fixed minimal spurion}

We now fix the first nondegenerate viable down-sector spurion to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
}
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
P_0(x)=\sum_{A=1}^3 p_A(x)\, z_A z_A^\dagger,
\qquad
p_A(x)=\frac{w_A(x)}{W(x)},
\qquad
w_A(x)=\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-X_A)^2}{2R^2}\right],
\qquad
W(x)=\sum_{B=1}^3 w_B(x),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
X_1=-1.5,\qquad X_2=0,\qquad X_3=1.8,
\end{equation}
the scalar down-sector profile is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d(x)=\mathrm{Tr}(T_dP_0(x))=p_1(x)-p_3(x)=\frac{w_1(x)-w_3(x)}{W(x)}.
}
\end{equation}

Its derivative can be written in two equivalent exact forms.

First,
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)=p_1'(x)-p_3'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}\Big[(X_1-\bar X(x))p_1(x)-(X_3-\bar X(x))p_3(x)\Big],
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\bar X(x)=\sum_{A=1}^3 X_A p_A(x).
\end{equation}

Second, using the exact pairwise link decomposition,
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)p_A(x)p_B(x),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
(t_1,t_2,t_3)=(1,0,-1),
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
(X_1-X_2)p_1p_2+(X_2-X_3)p_2p_3+2(X_1-X_3)p_1p_3
\Big].
}
\end{equation}
For the fixed centers,
\begin{equation}
X_1-X_2=-1.5,\qquad
X_2-X_3=-1.8,\qquad
X_1-X_3=-3.3,
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)
=
-\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1(x)p_2(x)+1.8\,p_2(x)p_3(x)+6.6\,p_1(x)p_3(x)
\Big].
}
\end{equation}
Since all \(p_Ap_B\ge 0\), this immediately implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)\le 0\qquad \text{for all }x.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Hermitian corrected operator}

The corrected toy operator is taken in the Hermitian form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\,\Pi_d(x)
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\}.
}
\end{equation}

Let the Gaussian basis be
\begin{equation}
b_\mu(x)=\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-Y_\mu)^2}{2\sigma_b^2}\right],
\qquad \mu=1,\dots,N_b.
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu\nu}:=\frac{Y_\mu+Y_\nu}{2},
\qquad
D_{\mu\nu}:=Y_\mu-Y_\nu,
\qquad
E_{\mu\nu}:=\exp\!\left[-\frac{D_{\mu\nu}^2}{4\sigma_b^2}\right].
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
b_\mu(x)b_\nu(x)=E_{\mu\nu}\exp\!\left[-\frac{(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2}{\sigma_b^2}\right].
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact Gaussian-basis matrix elements}

We write
\begin{equation}
Y^{(d)}=V+K,
\end{equation}
where \(V\) is the potential-like piece and \(K\) is the derivative transport piece.

\section{4. Potential part specialized to the minimal spurion}

The exact matrix element is
\begin{equation}
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\int dx\, b_\mu(x)\Pi_d(x)b_\nu(x)
=
g_d E_{\mu\nu}
\int dx\, e^{-(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2/\sigma_b^2}\Pi_d(x).
\end{equation}
Rescaling
\begin{equation}
x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u,
\qquad
dx=\sigma_b du,
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\,\sigma_b\,E_{\mu\nu}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}du\, e^{-u^2}
\Big[
p_1(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)-p_3(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u)
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Derivative part specialized to the minimal spurion}

The exact Hermitian form is
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
-\frac{i\kappa_d}{2}
\int dx\, \Pi_d'(x)\bigl(b_\mu b_\nu'-b_\mu' b_\nu\bigr).
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
b_\mu b_\nu'-b_\mu' b_\nu
=
\frac{Y_\nu-Y_\mu}{\sigma_b^2}b_\mu b_\nu,
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_b^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\int dx\, e^{-(x-M_{\mu\nu})^2/\sigma_b^2}\Pi_d'(x).
\end{equation}
After the rescaling \(x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_b}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}du\, e^{-u^2}\Pi_d'(M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u).
}
\end{equation}
Substituting the explicit \(\Pi_d'\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
=
-\,i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\int du\, e^{-u^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1p_2+1.8\,p_2p_3+6.6\,p_1p_3
\Big]_{x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u}.
}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\mu}=0.
}
\end{equation}
Thus the derivative term contributes only to off-diagonal transport in the Gaussian basis.

\section{6. Gauss--Hermite quadrature form}

Let \(\{\xi_n,\omega_n\}_{n=1}^{N_q}\) be the Gauss--Hermite nodes and weights for
\begin{equation}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}du\, e^{-u^2} f(u)\approx \sum_{n=1}^{N_q}\omega_n f(\xi_n).
\end{equation}
Define, for each matrix pair \((\mu,\nu)\),
\begin{equation}
x_{\mu\nu}^{(n)}:=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b \xi_n.
\end{equation}
At each quadrature point set
\begin{equation}
a_A^{(n)}:=-\frac{(x_{\mu\nu}^{(n)}-X_A)^2}{2R^2},
\qquad
m^{(n)}:=\max_A a_A^{(n)},
\end{equation}
and evaluate the stabilized exponentials
\begin{equation}
\tilde w_A^{(n)}:=e^{a_A^{(n)}-m^{(n)}},
\qquad
p_A^{(n)}:=\frac{\tilde w_A^{(n)}}{\tilde w_1^{(n)}+\tilde w_2^{(n)}+\tilde w_3^{(n)}}.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d^{(n)}=p_1^{(n)}-p_3^{(n)},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_d')^{(n)}
=
-\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1^{(n)}p_2^{(n)}
+
1.8\,p_2^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
+
6.6\,p_1^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
\Big].
}
\end{equation}
Therefore the matrix elements are evaluated numerically as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mu\nu}
\approx
g_d\,\sigma_b\,E_{\mu\nu}
\sum_{n=1}^{N_q}\omega_n \Pi_d^{(n)},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
\approx
i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_b}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\sum_{n=1}^{N_q}\omega_n (\Pi_d')^{(n)}.
}
\end{equation}
Substituting the explicit derivative profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{\mu\nu}
\approx
-\,i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\sum_{n=1}^{N_q}\omega_n
\Big[
1.5\,p_1^{(n)}p_2^{(n)}
+
1.8\,p_2^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
+
6.6\,p_1^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

This is the final execution-ready formula for the corrected minimal-spurion toy operator.

\section{7. Local Hessian basis and family projection}

Let the local toy Hessian be represented in the same Gaussian basis:
\begin{equation}
L_{\mu\nu}=\int dx\, b_\mu(x)\mathcal L_{\rm loc}b_\nu(x),
\qquad
S_{\mu\nu}=\int dx\, b_\mu(x)b_\nu(x).
\end{equation}
Since \(L\) and \(S\) are real symmetric, the generalized eigenproblem
\begin{equation}
Lc_A=\varepsilon_A S c_A
\end{equation}
admits a real eigenbasis. We choose the three family columns
\begin{equation}
C=(c_1,c_2,c_3),
\qquad
C^\dagger S C=I_3,
\end{equation}
with \(C\) real.

The projected family Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger Y^{(d)} C,
\qquad
Y^{(d)}=V+K.
}
\end{equation}
In components,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(H_d^{\rm fam})_{AB}
=
\sum_{\mu,\nu} C_{\mu A}\,Y_{\mu\nu}^{(d)}\,C_{\nu B},
\qquad
A,B=1,2,3.
}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Structural decomposition of \(H_d^{\rm fam}\)}

Because \(C\) is real, \(V\) is real symmetric, and \(K\) is purely imaginary antisymmetric, the family Hamiltonian has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d^{\rm fam}=D+R+iA,
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D=\text{real diagonal},
\qquad
R=\text{real symmetric off-diagonal part},
\qquad
A=\text{real antisymmetric}.
\end{equation}
Hence each off-diagonal family element is of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{AB}=r_{AB}+i a_{AB},
\qquad
r_{AB}=r_{BA}\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
a_{AB}=-a_{BA}\in\mathbb R.
}
\end{equation}

This is important for two reasons.

First, the derivative transport piece contributes directly to the imaginary off-diagonal entries.

Second, although a nontrivial rephasing-invariant phase is now \emph{allowed}, it is not yet \emph{guaranteed} by the present 1D minimal toy model alone.

\section{9. Why the hierarchy is still naturally expected}

For the minimal spurion,
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_d')^{(n)}
=
-\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1^{(n)}p_2^{(n)}
+
1.8\,p_2^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
+
6.6\,p_1^{(n)}p_3^{(n)}
\Big].
\end{equation}
The direct \(1\text{--}3\) coefficient is indeed largest at the raw coefficient level. However the associated profile \(p_1p_3\) is localized on the much longer link \(D_{13}=3.3\), and is therefore strongly suppressed compared with \(p_1p_2\) and \(p_2p_3\).

Thus the derivative contribution to the family Hamiltonian still obeys the qualitative expectation
\begin{equation}
|h_{13}^{(K)}|\ll |h_{12}^{(K)}|,\ |h_{23}^{(K)}|
\end{equation}
in the localized-family regime.

Moreover, the Gaussian basis overlap factor
\begin{equation}
E_{\mu\nu}=e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)}
\end{equation}
provides an additional suppression for long direct mixing. Therefore the corrected operator still has a built-in nearest-neighbor bias.

\section{10. Honest status at the end of this stage}

What is now rigorously closed is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{for }T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1),\ \Pi_d,\Pi_d',V_{\mu\nu},K_{\mu\nu}
\text{ are fully explicit and numerically executable.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger (V+K) C
\text{ is now a completely well-defined finite matrix computation.}
}
\end{equation}

What is not yet rigorously closed is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual CKM magnitudes have not yet been numerically extracted from this minimal-spurion run.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a nonzero rephasing-invariant CKM phase is allowed but not proven at the present 1D toy level.}
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the next step is no longer conceptual. It is the direct evaluation of the above quadratures and the computation of
\begin{equation}
d_1,d_2,d_3,\qquad h_{12},h_{23},h_{13},
\end{equation}
followed by the CKM extraction formulas.

\section{Final Summary}

We fixed the first nondegenerate viable toy down-sector spurion to
\begin{equation}
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
\end{equation}
For the three-defect background
\begin{equation}
P_0(x)=\sum_{A=1}^3 p_A(x)\, z_A z_A^\dagger,
\qquad
p_A(x)=\frac{e^{-(x-X_A)^2/(2R^2)}}{\sum_B e^{-(x-X_B)^2/(2R^2)}},
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
X_1=-1.5,\qquad X_2=0,\qquad X_3=1.8,
\end{equation}
the sector profile is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d(x)=p_1(x)-p_3(x),
\end{equation}
and its exact derivative is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
-\frac{1}{R^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1p_2+1.8\,p_2p_3+6.6\,p_1p_3
\Big].
\end{equation}

The Hermitian corrected toy operator is
\begin{equation}
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\,\Pi_d(x)
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d'(x),-i\partial_x\}.
\end{equation}
In the Gaussian basis
\begin{equation}
b_\mu(x)=e^{-(x-Y_\mu)^2/(2\sigma_b^2)},
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu\nu}=\frac{Y_\mu+Y_\nu}{2},
\qquad
D_{\mu\nu}=Y_\mu-Y_\nu,
\qquad
E_{\mu\nu}=e^{-D_{\mu\nu}^2/(4\sigma_b^2)},
\end{equation}
the execution-ready matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
V_{\mu\nu}
=
g_d\,\sigma_b\,E_{\mu\nu}
\int du\, e^{-u^2}\,[p_1-p_3]_{x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u},
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_{\mu\nu}
=
-\,i\,\frac{\kappa_d}{2\sigma_bR^2}(Y_\mu-Y_\nu)E_{\mu\nu}
\int du\, e^{-u^2}
\Big[
1.5\,p_1p_2+1.8\,p_2p_3+6.6\,p_1p_3
\Big]_{x=M_{\mu\nu}+\sigma_b u}.
\end{equation}
These integrals are directly evaluated by Gauss--Hermite quadrature.

If the generalized eigenbasis \(C\) is chosen real from
\begin{equation}
Lc_A=\varepsilon_A S c_A,
\qquad
C^\dagger S C=I_3,
\end{equation}
then the projected family Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_d^{\rm fam}=C^\dagger (V+K) C
\end{equation}
has the structural form
\begin{equation}
H_d^{\rm fam}=D+R+iA,
\end{equation}
with \(D\) real diagonal, \(R\) real symmetric, and \(A\) real antisymmetric.

Thus the corrected minimal-spurion toy model is now fully closed at the implementation level. The remaining open task is no longer operator definition, but the direct numerical extraction of
\begin{equation}
d_1,d_2,d_3,\qquad h_{12},h_{23},h_{13},
\end{equation}
and then the CKM observables from the resulting finite family Hamiltonian.

At the present stage, the nearest-neighbor hierarchy is structurally favored, while a nonzero physical CKM phase is allowed but not yet rigorously guaranteed by the 1D minimal toy model alone.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Status of the TECT Flavor/CKM Program: Proven Core, Conditional Layers, and the Remaining Frontier}

\section{1. Executive diagnosis}

The current direction of the TECT flavor program is fundamentally correct, but the proof status must be separated into three distinct layers:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) rigorously closed structural results,}\qquad
\text{(ii) conditionally supported effective constructions,}\qquad
\text{(iii) genuinely open microscopic realization problems.}
}
\end{equation}

The main point is that the research program is no longer blocked at the level of conceptual reduction. The actual frontier is now the microscopic realization step:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_0(x)\ \longrightarrow\ L_{\rm micro}[P_0]\ \longrightarrow\ \delta H_f^{\rm micro}[P_0]\ \longrightarrow\ H_f^{\rm fam}\ \longrightarrow\ V_{\rm CKM},\ \delta_{\rm CKM},\ J.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. What is rigorously closed}

\subsection{2.1. Reduction of the flavor problem to a finite family Hamiltonian}

Once a three-dimensional family subspace is isolated, the effective flavor operator is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_f
=
P_{\rm fam}\delta H_f P_{\rm fam}
-
P_{\rm fam}\delta H_f Q_{\rm fam}
\left(Q_{\rm fam}H_0Q_{\rm fam}-E_*\right)^{-1}
Q_{\rm fam}\delta H_f P_{\rm fam}
+
O(\delta H_f^3),
\end{equation}
and the family Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
(H_f^{\rm fam})_{AB}
=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal Y_f\phi_B\rangle.
\end{equation}
Therefore the leading flavor/CKM problem is rigorously reduced to a finite Hermitian matrix problem.

\subsection{2.2. CKM extraction from the family Hamiltonian}

In the basis where the up-sector is diagonal to leading order,
\begin{equation}
H_d^{\rm fam}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_1 & h_{12} & h_{13}\\
h_{12}^* & d_2 & h_{23}\\
h_{13}^* & h_{23}^* & d_3
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Delta_{ab}=d_a-d_b,
\end{equation}
and in the hierarchical regime one has
\begin{equation}
|V_{us}|
\simeq
\frac{|h_{12}|}{|\Delta_{21}|},
\qquad
|V_{cb}|
\simeq
\frac{|h_{23}|}{|\Delta_{32}|},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|V_{ub}|
\simeq
\left|
\frac{h_{13}}{\Delta_{31}}
-
\frac{h_{12}h_{23}}{\Delta_{21}\Delta_{31}}
\right|,
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
J
\simeq
\frac{\Im(h_{12}h_{23}h_{31})}{\Delta_{21}\Delta_{32}\Delta_{31}}.
\end{equation}
Thus the observable extraction formulas are not the bottleneck.

\subsection{2.3. Exact link decomposition of the corrected toy operator}

For a diagonal toy background
\begin{equation}
P_0(x)=\sum_A p_A(x)\,z_A z_A^\dagger,
\end{equation}
and a diagonal spurion
\begin{equation}
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(t_1,t_2,t_3),
\qquad
\Pi_d(x)=\mathrm{Tr}(T_dP_0)=\sum_A t_A p_A(x),
\end{equation}
one has the exact identity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}
\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)\,p_A(x)p_B(x).
}
\end{equation}
Hence the derivative-corrected transport term is exactly a sum over pairwise defect links.

\subsection{2.4. Exact spurion-selection constraint}

If \(t_A=t_B\), then the direct derivative link \(A\text{--}B\) vanishes identically. Therefore the degenerate spurion
\begin{equation}
T_d\propto \mathrm{diag}(2,-1,-1)
\end{equation}
eliminates the direct \(2\text{--}3\) derivative link and is not the correct first toy spurion for a clean CKM hierarchy study. The minimal viable first choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_d=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1).
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. What is only conditionally supported}

\subsection{3.1. The explicit toy multi-defect background}

The currently used background
\begin{equation}
P_0(x)=
\frac{\sum_A e^{-|x-X_A|^2/(2R^2)} z_A z_A^\dagger}
{\sum_B e^{-|x-X_B|^2/(2R^2)}}
\end{equation}
is a controlled and useful ansatz, but it has not yet been proven to be an actual solution of the microscopic Class II field equations.

\subsection{3.2. The toy local Hessian}

The operator
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm loc}=-Z\nabla^2+\mu^2+2\lambda \rho(x)
\end{equation}
is a plausible effective localization operator, but it is not yet the fully derived microscopic second variation of the Class II action.

\subsection{3.3. The corrected toy down-sector operator}

The Hermitian surrogate
\begin{equation}
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\Pi_d
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d',-i\partial_x\}
\end{equation}
is structurally well-motivated and successfully repairs the long-link contamination of the older potential-like toy model, but it has not yet been uniquely derived from the microscopic UV/Class II sector coupling.

\subsection{3.4. Localized-family asymptotics}

The scaling estimate
\begin{equation}
|h_{AB}^{(K)}|
\asymp
|t_A-t_B|D_{AB}^2 e^{-\alpha D_{AB}^2}
\end{equation}
is valid in the localized-family regime, but it is not a global theorem without localization assumptions.

\section{4. What remains genuinely open}

The genuinely open frontier is the microscopic realization problem:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct or prove the existence of an actual Class II multi-defect background \(P_0\),
\item derive the true microscopic Hessian \(L_{\rm micro}[P_0]\),
\item derive the true sector operators \(\delta H_f^{\rm micro}[P_0]\),
\item compute the projected matrices \(H_u^{\rm fam}\) and \(H_d^{\rm fam}\),
\item extract the actual CKM hierarchy and determine whether \(J\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}

In particular, the present 1D minimal toy model structurally favors the hierarchy
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}|,\ |h_{23}| \gg |h_{13}|,
\end{equation}
but it does not yet rigorously guarantee a nonzero physical CKM phase.

\section{5. Strategic conclusion}

The current direction is correct because the finite-family reduction is already closed. The remaining work is not to search for a different conceptual route, but to replace the current toy inputs by microscopic Class II-derived inputs in the chain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_0
\;\to\;
L_{\rm micro}
\;\to\;
\delta H_f^{\rm micro}
\;\to\;
H_f^{\rm fam}
\;\to\;
V_{\rm CKM},\delta_{\rm CKM},J.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the next rigorous program is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{actual background construction}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{actual Hessian extraction}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{actual sector-operator derivation}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{CKM computation}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The TECT flavor/CKM program is presently in the following state.

What is rigorously closed is the structural reduction:
once a three-dimensional family subspace exists, the flavor problem reduces to a finite Hermitian family Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
(H_f^{\rm fam})_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal Y_f\phi_B\rangle,
\end{equation}
and the CKM observables are read off from this matrix by standard perturbative formulas.

At the toy operator level, a genuinely strong exact result has also been established:
for a diagonal spurion \(T_d=\mathrm{diag}(t_1,t_2,t_3)\), the derivative profile satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Pi_d'(x)
=
\frac{1}{R^2}\sum_{A<B}(t_A-t_B)(X_A-X_B)p_A(x)p_B(x),
\end{equation}
so the corrected transport term is exactly a sum over pairwise defect links. This explains why the corrected toy operator suppresses the direct long \(1\text{--}3\) mixing relative to nearest-neighbor transport.

What is not yet rigorously closed is the microscopic realization of these ingredients. The currently used multi-defect background \(P_0\), the local Hessian \(\mathcal L_{\rm loc}\), and the corrected toy sector operator
\begin{equation}
\delta H_d^{\rm herm}
=
g_d\Pi_d
+
\frac{\kappa_d}{2}\{\Pi_d',-i\partial_x\}
\end{equation}
are all effective constructions, not yet fully derived uniquely from the Class II microscopic theory.

Therefore the present direction is correct, but the frontier has shifted. The remaining work is no longer conceptual reduction, but microscopic realization:
\begin{equation}
P_0
\;\to\;
L_{\rm micro}
\;\to\;
\delta H_f^{\rm micro}
\;\to\;
H_f^{\rm fam}
\;\to\;
V_{\rm CKM},\delta_{\rm CKM},J.
\end{equation}

The immediate rigorous program should therefore be:
\begin{equation}
\text{(i) construct or justify the actual Class II background,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(ii) derive the actual microscopic Hessian,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(iii) derive the actual sector operators,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(iv) compute the projected family Hamiltonians and extract CKM data.}
\end{equation}

In short:
the backbone of the flavor program is already proven,
the current toy operator program is a strong and useful effective bridge,
but the decisive remaining proofs are the microscopic background, the microscopic Hessian, and the microscopic sector couplings.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Preconditions for a Physically Meaningful CKM Computation in TECT}

\section{1. Purpose}

Before performing a direct CKM extraction, one must first isolate the minimal conditions under which the projected family Hamiltonians can be interpreted as physical quark flavor data rather than as basis-dependent toy matrices.

\section{2. Minimal preconditions}

A physically meaningful CKM computation requires at least the following five conditions.

\subsection{2.1. Common left-handed family subspace}

There must exist a common three-dimensional family subspace
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}=\mathrm{span}\{\phi_A\}_{A=1}^3
\end{equation}
on which both the up-sector and down-sector operators act. Without a common family space, the relative unitary misalignment defining CKM is not well-defined.

\subsection{2.2. Canonical kinetic normalization}

After projection to the family sector, the kinetic form must be reduced to the canonical identity:
\begin{equation}
Z_{AB}\;\to\;\delta_{AB}.
\end{equation}
Otherwise the naive diagonalization of the projected Hamiltonians does not yet yield the physical mixing matrix.

\subsection{2.3. Nondegenerate diagonal splittings}

The projected family Hamiltonians
\begin{equation}
H_u^{\rm fam},\qquad H_d^{\rm fam}
\end{equation}
must have nondegenerate diagonal splittings:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{21}\neq 0,\qquad \Delta_{32}\neq 0,\qquad \Delta_{31}\neq 0.
\end{equation}
Without this, the perturbative CKM formulas are ill-defined.

\subsection{2.4. Hierarchy seed in the off-diagonal structure}

The family Hamiltonian must structurally favor the ordering
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}|,\ |h_{23}| \gg |h_{13}|,
\end{equation}
or more sharply in the desired regime,
\begin{equation}
|h_{12}|>|h_{23}|>|h_{13}|.
\end{equation}
Otherwise the observed CKM hierarchy has no microscopic seed.

\subsection{2.5. Irreducible CP seed}

There must exist at least one phase source that cannot be removed by family rephasings, so that
\begin{equation}
\Im(h_{12}h_{23}h_{31})\neq 0
\end{equation}
is possible. A purely one-dimensional toy model with a single commuting diagonal spurion may fail this requirement even if it reproduces the hierarchy pattern.

\section{3. Strategic consequence}

Therefore the correct order of work is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{minimal CKM preconditions}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{verification of each condition}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{direct CKM extraction}.
}
\end{equation}

The immediate next task is not yet the final CKM fit itself, but the rigorous classification of which of these five conditions are already closed, which are conditionally supported, and which remain open.

\section{Final Summary}

Yes: before pushing further into direct CKM extraction, it is preferable to fix the minimal preconditions that make such an extraction physically meaningful.

The necessary minimal conditions are:
\begin{equation}
\text{(i) a common left-handed family subspace,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(ii) canonical kinetic normalization,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(iii) nondegenerate diagonal splittings,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(iv) an off-diagonal hierarchy seed,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\text{(v) an irreducible CP-violating phase seed.}
\end{equation}

Without these conditions, a projected toy family Hamiltonian cannot yet be interpreted as a physically meaningful CKM matrix. Therefore the correct next step is to organize these conditions explicitly and determine which are already established, which are only conditionally supported, and which remain open.
